  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_79e39775-ba9d-4f91-9c6b-988168979463'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText7058845238693580695" style="display:none"><i>Once upon a time, I was a little girl who disappeared. <br /> <br /> Once upon a time, my name was not Alice. <br /> <br /> Once upon a time, I didn't know how lucky I was.</i> <br /><br /> When Alice was ten, Ray took her away from her family, her friends -- her life. <div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/50938238-shannon-fay"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1451740716i/50938238._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/50938238-shannon-fay">Shannon Fay</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    She was shot in the stomach. Like the other answer says, Jake shot twice. One bullet hit Ray, the other hit Alice. <br />"...the pain in my stomach is great<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    She was shot in the stomach. Like the other answer says, Jake shot twice. One bullet hit Ray, the other hit Alice. <br />"...the pain in my stomach is greater than the one in my shoulder..." indicating that her stomach is REALLY injured, cuz she'd already been stabbed in the shoulder. <br />"[Jake] touches my side and lifts up fingers dark like night" (they're covered in her blood).<br />"'Oh no,' he says" (because he realizes he shot her)<br />"I don't have to close my eyes to sleep now it is coming for me" <br /><br />Sadly, she definitely dies, and while it's tragic, the silver lining is that she's finally free.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9941088948859071875">I probably would have liked this book more if i were a teenager or a pedophile. I mostly just read this for science. it came up in my collection development class when we were talking about challenged books (that doesn't mean that they are handicapped, but that they have been rarrred at by angry parents and other scared concerned types), but when i heard what it was about - i pretty much had to read it to see how an author handled this situation, because it seemed rough stuff for teen fiction. t</span>
  <span id="freeText9941088948859071875" style="display:none">I probably would have liked this book more if i were a teenager or a pedophile. I mostly just read this for science. it came up in my collection development class when we were talking about challenged books (that doesn't mean that they are handicapped, but that they have been rarrred at by angry parents and other scared concerned types), but when i heard what it was about - i pretty much had to read it to see how an author handled this situation, because it seemed rough stuff for teen fiction. the basic premise - although i hate doing plot summaries - is that "alice" (the first-person narrator)is kidnapped when she is ten and physically and sexually abused for 5 years, but when she starts to develop physically beyond her captor's personal preference, he enlists her help in selecting her own replacement. so -ew. and i don't know anything about psychology, child or otherwise, so i don't know the terminology, but she just completely shuts down, emotionally, into a not-quite-stockholm syndrome - she doesn't align herself with him for anything but self-preservation, but she has just given up fighting and does what he wants, because he has made threats about hurting her family etc. so - she has all this freedom to leave the house and go to the park to find this new-child for him, but she can't do anything to save herself, which is very frustrating for the reader.The author gets 5 stars for balls - for tackling the subject matter to begin with and for the ending which i'm sure had some people up in startled emotional flight mode.and as a cautionary tale, it should also get 5 stars, although a teen audience is a little old for the caution, and any younger readers would be traumatized beyond therapy. do not give this book to your 8-year-old. just tell them to stay away from unmarked vans. i just personally didn't connect to it. the subject matter is horrifying, but in the abstract, and this character's shutdown response didn't make me want to save her so much as walk in, splash some water on her and say "snap out of it". when i was little, these were my literary kidnapping equivalents:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380332314i/692889.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380332314i/692890._SY540_.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and they were way more gentle in terms of what the girls went through, wayyyy fewer forced blowjobs, but it gave me a total sense of confidence - if i got my ass kidnapped, i could get out of it with my cleverness. i used to dream about being kidnapped, and the ways i would elude my tormentors. it's probably a really good thing i was never actually kidnapped, because this here book is probably closer to the reality - feisty kids don't always win, but this might have made me a little more of a shut-in, and may have ruined my devil-may-care years, so i would have lost some good adventure-stories. i didn't personally love this book, but there's no reason it shouldn't be in a library. libraries are full of books. you don't like this one, don't write an angry letter, just go read another one. hell, <i>i'm</i> about to.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9941088948859071875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_169247466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169247466" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169247466?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Wendy Darling by: </span>
      Ginny
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=to-acquire-arc-or-pb">to-acquire-arc-or-pb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=tough-subjects">tough-subjects</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=made-my-heart-hurt">made-my-heart-hurt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=mature-ya">mature-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169247466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3942226523302878258">Is it possible to write a story about a child being imprisoned and make it gut-wrenching and relevant? After the disappointment of various different books I've read recently involving kidnapping and child endangerment, I wasn't sure, particularly when it comes to the YA genre. But after reading <i>Living Dead Girl</i>, I have my answer: it's yes. Resoundingly, unequivocally, yes.<br/><br/>15-year-old "Alice" has lived with Ray since she was 10. Kidnapped from a school field trip and taken to Shady Pines Apartmen</span>
  <span id="freeText3942226523302878258" style="display:none">Is it possible to write a story about a child being imprisoned and make it gut-wrenching and relevant? After the disappointment of various different books I've read recently involving kidnapping and child endangerment, I wasn't sure, particularly when it comes to the YA genre. But after reading <i>Living Dead Girl</i>, I have my answer: it's yes. Resoundingly, unequivocally, yes.<br /><br />15-year-old "Alice" has lived with Ray since she was 10. Kidnapped from a school field trip and taken to Shady Pines Apartments, she lives among ordinary people who don't really see her or don't really want to. Every day Ray cuddles her on his lap and forces her to submit to him, punishing her with his fists and his words if she does anything to displease him. Her attempts to defy him--including one botched escape--are met with out-of-control violence until her resistance is completely beaten down. <br /><br />This is not an easy book to read. While it is not explicit, the terrible things that Alice is subjected to are not glossed over. I've seen some criticisms that the book goes overboard in describing what she is forced to do, but I disagree. The reality is that there are children out there who have been and no doubt currently are subjected to this kind of torture, and the description and repetition of these acts helps us to understand in some small way what victims have to go through. I never thought the descriptions crossed the line in terms of tastelessness or exploitation.<br /><br />The author does an incredible job of describing Alice's terror and confusion, as well as her eventual numbness. There are many details worked into the story that have a ring of truth, including the dull repetition of her days watching tv, the anxiety when Ray comes home, the punishments meted out for small infractions, the attempts to keep her small and childlike, Alice's lank appearance and poor circulation from lack of nutrition, etc. Most importantly, the author touches on the way abuse tends to perpetrate more abuse and the awful resignation that Alice begins to feel to her plight.<br /><br /><i>I don't understand why my shell keeps living. Breathing. Why won't it listen to me, to the little part I have that isn't Ray, to that tiny once upon a time girl who just wants to close her eyes and never wake up again?</i><br /><br />There were so many details that made me hurt with empathy for Alice, not only in relation to her sexual abuse, but also in relation to the way Ray starves her as a means to control her and to keep her from growing up. The descriptions of her sharp hunger after days of eating practically nothing were heart-wrenching. Alice describes tasting a sandwich with <i>"not one, but two slices of...salty cheese and slippery ham and cottony bread, so light in my mouth. I could eat these forever, until the world ended and beyond."</i> <br /><br />I have a great deal of admiration for the author for writing about this subject with such restraint and sympathy. This isn't a perfect book--I thought the "once upon a time" device was repetitious and not entirely successful--but it is a searingly memorable one that handles a difficult subject with great skill. I don't feel that "serious" books that are primarily about kidnapping and imprisonment are enjoyable for the sake of pure entertainment, and that's the primary objection I have to the fictional books I've previously read that deal with this subject. I go into this more in my review of the disappointing and much-lauded <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143570981" rel="nofollow noopener">Room</a>, but suffice to say that what I hope to gain from reading about such unhappy subjects are some degree of insight (into both the victim's suffering and the perpetrator's motivation) as well as a great deal of empathy. I got both in spades with <i>Living Dead Girl</i>.<br /><br /><b>Recommended for adults or mature teens only.</b><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3942226523302878258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_168589051" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168589051" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168589051?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416960607" href="/book/show/6413444-living-dead-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168589051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17721620283126404603"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Well, the book leaves scars I can definitely tell you that much. I didn't know quite what to expect from this book, all I'd heard about it previously was that it's a story about abuse and a very short read (170 pages, large writing in my edition). I'd heard reviewers describe it as 'disturbing', but I didn't dwell on that too much, I assumed that when you've read a couple of Stephen King's books (namely <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1131777.It' rel='nofollow noopener'>It</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10614.Misery' rel='nofollow noopener'>Misery</a>, etc.) you'd pretty much got your heard around 'disturbing'.<br/><br/>I was wrong. The a</span>
  <span id="freeText17721620283126404603" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Well, the book leaves scars I can definitely tell you that much. I didn't know quite what to expect from this book, all I'd heard about it previously was that it's a story about abuse and a very short read (170 pages, large writing in my edition). I'd heard reviewers describe it as 'disturbing', but I didn't dwell on that too much, I assumed that when you've read a couple of Stephen King's books (namely <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1131777.It" rel="nofollow noopener">It</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10614.Misery" rel="nofollow noopener">Misery</a>, etc.) you'd pretty much got your heard around 'disturbing'.<br><br>I was wrong. The author draws you in with her unique and just plain strange writing style, despite being weird it's also very effective. It takes us deep inside the mind of a person who has not only suffered extreme physical and sexual abuse (though there's been plenty of that) but has also been so psychologically damaged that her hope is only for death to come swiftly, she is so desperate that she is even willing to sacrifice a young girl to make her suffering end. And, awful as that is, I couldn't hate her for it.<br><br>I've read a number of books where the first person narrative is by someone mentally damaged; some work (e.g. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6514" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bell Jar</a>), most do not. Scott's not only worked, but affected me deeply. I could also see how Ray's past experiences of abuse and a loveless childhood had made him the monster he was, he was never meant to be redeemed, but perhaps understood to some extent. The entire story was very fast, very horrifying and completely unforgettable. My first thoughts when I put it down were "I have to get someone else to read this now", despite it not being something I'd normally go about recommending to friends with a casual "enjoy!" thrown in.<br><br>It's labelled a young adult novel, god knows why but it is. This book would have given me nightmares a few years ago - and it may well give me nightmares tonight. I don't think for one second that this is particularly a children/teenage story, in fact it's debatable as to whether or not it's actually suitable for them at all. The writing itself is neither simplistic or teen/child-oriented, but deep and complex.<br><br>I certainly won't forget this book, whether or not that's a good thing though, remains undecided.</span>

<div id="review_1081551206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1081551206" />
    <a title="Irena BookDustMagic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic"><img alt="Irena BookDustMagic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362943196p2/17737927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1081551206?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irena BookDustMagic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irena BookDustMagic" href="/user/show/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic">Irena BookDustMagic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic?shelf=2014-contemporary-challenge">2014-contemporary-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1081551206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1167947045840881305"><b>Edit: the pedophile I'm talking about in my review died this year (2019).</b><br/><br/>I came across this book one day watching some BookTube video named "All Time Favorites". It's blurb got me interested so I bought it but haven't picked it up for a couple of months.<br/><br/>Yesterday, I didn't feel like reading any book I already started but didn't want to commit myself to another one, so this book seemed like an obvious choice because it's pretty short.<br/><br/><b>I finished this book in a day but it's story will stuck with me</b></span>
  <span id="freeText1167947045840881305" style="display:none"><b>Edit: the pedophile I'm talking about in my review died this year (2019).</b><br /><br />I came across this book one day watching some BookTube video named "All Time Favorites". It's blurb got me interested so I bought it but haven't picked it up for a couple of months.<br /><br />Yesterday, I didn't feel like reading any book I already started but didn't want to commit myself to another one, so this book seemed like an obvious choice because it's pretty short.<br /><br /><b>I finished this book in a day but it's story will stuck with me for a long, long time. I hope it will stuck forever.</b><br /><br />Unfortunately, I can't say it was an eye opener. Since I was a not so little but still little girl I knew this world is populated with pedophiles. I spend days and days with my little girlfriends playing in the yard of one. Petting his dogs and eating candies he would give to us.<br />I had an older sister to figure out his intentions. I had Sister in my church to tell me that we children have to tell someone how he is acting when we are with him when grown ups weren't around.<br />Still, somehow, we thought telling it would be wrong. somehow, we were scared of what would it happen' if we tell someone.<br /><br />I had "luck" and he didn't do any physical abuse to me, but not all my friends had the same "luck" (although I still remember all those pictures and posters full with naked ladies he showed to us once).<br />Two of my friends he forced to french kiss him when he got them alone. Other two, sisters, he not only forced them into kissing, he touched them.<br />Not one of them told their parents, and nobody ever sued him. <br /><br />Today, he is still a free man, thank God too sick to go out of his house, but still, he got away with everything.<br />We were not the first generation he "played" with. Later, we found out what he did to us, he already did to one of my girlfriend's mom.<br />Still, she had let her daughter to go in his yard. She thought her daughter is safe as long as she is not all alone with him.<br />And everyone kept quiet about our neighbor pedophile.<br />Nobody was brave enough to accuse him because he didn't actually rape anyone.<br />I wonder if that is even true.<br /><br />I feel like me and my sister are the only ones who are calling him how he deserves to be called: <b>a pedophile. Because he is one, no matter if he didn't actually rape anyone.</b> At least not that we know of.<br /><br />Still, as we do that, we are the ones others are looking at like we do something wrong. Not him.<br />He got away.<br />Because of everyone who knew and did nothing. Including myself and my sister. Because we didn't do any legal accusation after we became adults, and now the statute of limitations is in power.<br />We missed our chance.<br /><br />What this book did to me, it reminded me how people are turning their heads off when someone needs them to look, to see.<br />I really, really hope everyone will read this or similar book at some point of their lives and they will open their eyes and look. And if they see, they will tell out loud in the world that monster is among them.<br />I hope people will realize that by protecting the monster, we become one as well.<br /><br /><b>This is the work of fiction, but trust me, the world is full of Alices and Rays. They are real. Now. In this moment. In this world.<br />Don't look away.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1167947045840881305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27671553?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27671553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8397204078023263117">Elizabeth Scott is a genius. A literary genius. I’ve read some of Elizabeth’s other titles, and I find myself wondering, how can these be written by the same person. And I don’t mean that in a Stephenie Meyer/<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162543.Breaking_Dawn__The_Twilight_Saga__Book_4_' title='Breaking Dawn (The Twilight Saga, Book 4) by Stephenie Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Breaking Dawn</a> way. To have that kind of diverse talent, it is simply effing amazing. <br/><br/>I read this book in one setting. It is truly powerful. The emotion– sadness, despair it’s so apparent it’s freaky. How can I say that I loved a book about abduction, sexual abuse, and suffering? Why do you </span>
  <span id="freeText8397204078023263117" style="display:none">Elizabeth Scott is a genius. A literary genius. I’ve read some of Elizabeth’s other titles, and I find myself wondering, how can these be written by the same person. And I don’t mean that in a Stephenie Meyer/<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162543.Breaking_Dawn__The_Twilight_Saga__Book_4_" title="Breaking Dawn (The Twilight Saga, Book 4) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Breaking Dawn</a> way. To have that kind of diverse talent, it is simply effing amazing. <br /><br />I read this book in one setting. It is truly powerful. The emotion– sadness, despair it’s so apparent it’s freaky. How can I say that I loved a book about abduction, sexual abuse, and suffering? Why do you look out your car window when you drive by the scene of an accident, do you want to see a dead, possibly mutilated body? But I did, I loved it. It was a masterpiece. And not because of what it was about, but because of how it made me feel. <br /><br />It’s gripping, enthralling and completely horrifying. The most disturbing parts aren’t even written, but left to the reader to fill in the sickening details. I’ve read suggestions that this book shouldn’t be targeted to a teen audience. Why? Because ignorance is bliss? Because we don’t need to add to the things that teenagers are desensitized from? Don’t worry if you ignore the situation it will go away. That’s how our society deals with those things, right? Just sweep it under the rug. No one will have to know that the world is a dirty place. Do you ever have one of those moments where you want to let out a good frustrated scream... yeah, this is one of those times.... <br /><br />Elizabeth Scott you’re my hero. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8397204078023263117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1287228519" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1287228519?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✦❋Arianna✦❋" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna">✦❋Arianna✦❋</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416960607" href="/book/show/6413444-living-dead-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23370948-arianna?shelf=dark-romance">dark-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1287228519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1204384287331193183"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433170596i/15058369._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='550' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I look wrong.<br/> 	I look dead.<br/> 	I'm not, though. I'm only partway there, a living dead girl.<br/> 	I have been for five years.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>‘Alice’ is a 15 years old girl who was kidnapped when she was 10 and taken to Shady Pines Apartments. She lives with her captor, Ray, who pretends they are father and daughter. But Ray doesn’t treat ‘Alice’ like a daughter. He abuses her in every way possible, calling her ‘his little girl’, demanding to be a good girl for her daddy. Alice learnt the hard way that sh</span>
  <span id="freeText1204384287331193183" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433170596i/15058369._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="550" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I look wrong.<br> 	I look dead.<br> 	I'm not, though. I'm only partway there, a living dead girl.<br> 	I have been for five years.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>‘Alice’ is a 15 years old girl who was kidnapped when she was 10 and taken to Shady Pines Apartments. She lives with her captor, Ray, who pretends they are father and daughter. But Ray doesn’t treat ‘Alice’ like a daughter. He abuses her in every way possible, calling her ‘his little girl’, demanding to be a good girl for her daddy. Alice learnt the hard way that she’s alone in all this. Her neighbors choose not to notice there’s something strange is going on in their home or that Ray is a sick psycho. No one sees her. Alice ‘accepts’ all this because she wants to protect her parents. She wants them to stay alive, to have a life. However, she tried to escape once, but her situation got worse, Ray becoming more abusive. <br><br>This was a dark, gritty, disturbing read and I definitely not enjoyed it. It felt more real than other reads since we all know things like this happens all the time. My heart broke for Alice. She’s so psychologically damaged, so afraid and so confused at times. She’s only 15 years old, but at times she felt more mature than that. Well, I guess all the abuse she suffered over the years changed her. She wants to be ‘free’ so badly that she agrees at some point to help Ray to kidnap a little girl. She wants to survive and she’s ready to do anything to stop her suffering. The internal conflict is done well and despite everything I really understand ‘Alice’. She only wants to survive.<br> <br>The writing style was unique, the story fast paced and gripping, yet gut-wrenching and haunting.<br><br>Overall, a great read!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I thought living dead girls couldn't feel pain, thought I was emptied out but I'm not, I'm not.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_31849139" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31849139" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1066511-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518107210p2/1066511.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31849139?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/1066511-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">mature teenagers, adults</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066511-julie?shelf=2008">2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066511-julie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066511-julie?shelf=signed-out">signed-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066511-julie?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066511-julie?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31849139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4133578972430576034">This book is amazing. I picked it up on a whim, one of the few YA books we had enough copies of at work for me to borrow. <i>Living Dead Girl</i> tells a chilling story from the perspective of "Alice," a 15-year-old who was abducted at age 10 by a man named Ray, who proceeds to spend 5 years molding her into the perfect object of his desire, both physically and mentally.<br/><br/>The book is incredibly disturbing - as it should be. I wanted the entire time to just run to where she was, break the door down and ge</span>
  <span id="freeText4133578972430576034" style="display:none">This book is amazing. I picked it up on a whim, one of the few YA books we had enough copies of at work for me to borrow. <i>Living Dead Girl</i> tells a chilling story from the perspective of "Alice," a 15-year-old who was abducted at age 10 by a man named Ray, who proceeds to spend 5 years molding her into the perfect object of his desire, both physically and mentally.<br /><br />The book is incredibly disturbing - as it should be. I wanted the entire time to just run to where she was, break the door down and get her out of there. I think what makes it so intense is watching "Alice" go from complete despair to find a thin, tiny thread of hope... and what results.<br /><br />It is chilling to watch her helping to plot the abduction of another girl - even younger this time - she is SO willing to help commit another terrible act just to get her abductor's attention away from her.<br /><br />The end is scary, dramatic, disturbing, triumphant - all rightfully so, and brought a jarring close to the story of "Alice." And yet, I'm happy for her...<br /><br />It's hard to say who I'd recommend this book to, exactly. It's definitely very difficult, disturbing subject matter. I would mostly say adults should read it rather than teenagers. I think it is a cry for help for ALL children trapped in this kind of situation. It's a cry for everyone to pay attention to what is going on around them, ask questions, don't just shrug off your suspicions. People in these situations often cannot fend for themselves, or make the move to free themselves, so others need to be more proactive in watching for the signs.<br /><br />All in all, this book greatly affected me, and I'd definitely recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4133578972430576034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_66783908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66783908" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66783908?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781423397519" href="/book/show/6299078-living-dead-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66783908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9404517380083495278">Well, people who have told me that "Living Dead Girl" was a horrifying book were absolutely correct. This is definitely one of the most depressing and scary stories I have ever read. Basically every sentence of this novel is a painful assault on your psyche. The descriptions of daily physical, psychological and sexual abuse are almost impossible to bear.<br/><br/>I have to give Elizabeth Scott kudos for creating a very realistic in its atrociousness story that won't leave anyone untouched. The despicable </span>
  <span id="freeText9404517380083495278" style="display:none">Well, people who have told me that "Living Dead Girl" was a horrifying book were absolutely correct. This is definitely one of the most depressing and scary stories I have ever read. Basically every sentence of this novel is a painful assault on your psyche. The descriptions of daily physical, psychological and sexual abuse are almost impossible to bear.<br /><br />I have to give Elizabeth Scott kudos for creating a very realistic in its atrociousness story that won't leave anyone untouched. The despicable routine of Alice's existence is mortifying; her complete defeat and her willingness to put another child in her own place just to get some peace (even if that peace equals death) are awfully terrifying and yet strangely understandable; the portrayal of Alice's abuser with his broken childhood and his twisted view of love rings true as well. It is obvious Scott has done her research and got a great grasp of psyches of both the abuser and the abused. <br /><br />However if I were ever to talk to the writer of "Living Dead Girl," I would tell her that if you create a disturbing story like this, if you take your readers on such an emotional roller-coaster, you'd better come up with a better ending than the one we were offered. If there is no hope or inspiration, such a tale becomes simply a horror story with nothing to learn, an exercise at psychological manipulation if you will. <br /><br />But my major problem with this book is that it is written for young adults. I don't quite understand the purpose of subjecting kids to this kind of story. It is definitely not a cautionary tale (as it might be for adults) as they would be too old for that and it sure doesn't teach them any lessons. The only thing this book will achieve is to scare them out of their sleep due to endless depictions of various assaults which in spite of their vagueness are quite graphic.<br /><br />Overall, "Living Dead Girl" is a memorable albeit painful read. Not the book I would widely recommend and certainly not the one for younger readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9404517380083495278" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_145256638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145256638" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1859184-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524741556p2/1859184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145256638?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/1859184-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1859184-emily?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1859184-emily?shelf=tragedy">tragedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1859184-emily?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer145256638&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145256638" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5308072843746134265">UGH. I never had any intention of reading this book until Bitch Magazine posted a list of Feminist YA books on their website this weekend and, much to my surprise, this was on it. I questioned its place on the list, a staffer said they'd look into it, and I second guessed myself. Turns out I was right the first time: this isn't feminist at all. What's more, I'd say that this is the literary equivalent of torture porn, except worse than anything you'll actually ever see on the big screen; this bo</span>
  <span id="freeText5308072843746134265" style="display:none">UGH. I never had any intention of reading this book until Bitch Magazine posted a list of Feminist YA books on their website this weekend and, much to my surprise, this was on it. I questioned its place on the list, a staffer said they'd look into it, and I second guessed myself. Turns out I was right the first time: this isn't feminist at all. What's more, I'd say that this is the literary equivalent of torture porn, except worse than anything you'll actually ever see on the big screen; this book has no redeeming social value whatsoever.<br /><br />(Edited a week later to add some thoughts I've better developed since discussing with librarian buddies who both love and hate this book.)<br /><br />I can't deny that this book will appeal to horror-hungry teens, and as a librarian I have to give it credit for that. But frankly, it is ONLY as a genre horror novel that I can give it credit. Same way I don't want to watch Hostel, I don't want to read books like this. Clearly some people do, so however much I personally might have hated the experience of reading it, I can accept that this is a different strokes kind of thing. But I have a real problem with this book being marketed as anything other than horror. It SHOCKS me that anyone could call this a feminist work. <br /><br />Does it make sense to say that the bleakness of this book makes it pointless? I just wonder, what does a teen reader, or any reader, have to hold onto at the end? Kyla is already apparently damaged beyond repair when the book begins, completely broken and tragic, but well on her way to monstrous, too: using her own sexuality to control others who she perceives as being weak; viciously mean when she has the opportunity to be; positively gleeful over the thought of freeing herself at the cost of another girl's freedom. It seems to me that with the ending she gives us, Scott lazily skirts around the possibility of recovery, of any possible empowerment or justice. And I'm not someone who thinks every book should have a happy (or even optimistic) ending, I just think that THIS book becomes pointless without one. There's no story here -- this is a completely bleak and voyeuristic snapshot of horrific abuse and NOTHING ELSE, merely something you tell little girls to scare them into submission. I think, in the end, a reader has nothing to gain from this book except for a good scare (which it certainly delivers), and I think that does discredit it, pretty much entirely, as a piece of serious literary fiction. <br /><br />I will say that I thought Scott's writing was much, much better here than in the very boring and awkward Perfect You (except for the dialog, which this author cannot write at all). <br /><br />But all in all I was happier person before I read this, and the world was probably a better place before it was written. Yuck. A million yucks. I want a shower. <br /><br />For a better, smarter captor/captive book, try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7937843.Room" title="Room by Emma Donoghue" rel="nofollow noopener">Room</a>. For a better, smarter abuse book, try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71332.Push" title="Push by Sapphire" rel="nofollow noopener">Push</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5308072843746134265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13412222133571718381" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“I decide everything. Remember that.” God and monster all in one, and mine to worship.</i>
</b><br><br>First of all . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512058979ra/24568254.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Well, minus the crying. This was rough, but it takes more than a brutal storyline to get me to squirt some tears (more specifically, my period). <i>Living Dead Girl</i> is about – here I’ll just let the book tell you . . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“Once upon a time, I did not live in Shady Pines. Once upon a time, my name was not Alice. Once upon a time, I didn’t know how lucky I was.”</i>
</b><br><br>When Alice was 10 years old, her class took a field trip to the local aquarium. Alice got separated from everyone after being disappointed in the lack of dolphins and opting to go see the penguins on her own. It was there that she met a gentlemen who informed her that her class was now watching a movie and he would show her to the theater. Five years have passed since that day. Five years since Alice has seen her mother and father. Five years since she last saw her house at 623 Daisy Lane. Five years of living with Ray . . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“You can get used to anything. You think you can’t, you want to die, but you don’t. You won’t. You just are.”</i>
</b><br><br>I had never even heard of this book until over the weekend and I’ll be damned if I can remember what “if you liked this, you should try THIS” list it popped up on over at the Faceplace, but I am completely blown away I haven’t seen it over and over again on the Banned Books Week suggestions. To whoever decided to market this as a Young Adult selection, I give you mad props because you must have balls the size of watermelons. I can only assume the pitch was something of a “think of this like a modernized after school special.” <br><br><i>Living Dead Girl</i> is definitely a story each parent will have to decide for themselves if they think their child should read (and I encourage parents to read this first before allowing your kid to check it out). While there are not necessarily specific <i>details</i> given regarding the abuse Alice suffers, that does not make the story less graphic and two-and-two is easily put together regarding all of the goings on. As the story progresses there’s a solid chance questions will arise about some of Alice’s behaviors and what she is willing to do in order to no longer be the focus of Ray’s attention. Not to mention that, much like in real life, a tale like this cannot have a happy ending. Assuming my children would actually read on their own voluntarily, I would probably attempt to keep this one off their TBR until high school. Highly recommended to anyone who thinks they can handle it and zero judgment for anyone who knows they can't.</span>

<div id="review_52705106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52705106" />
    <a title="Trudi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1416912-trudi"><img alt="Trudi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446613110p2/1416912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52705106?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trudi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trudi" href="/user/show/1416912-trudi">Trudi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=pass-the-kleenex">pass-the-kleenex</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=modern-lit">modern-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=traumatizing">traumatizing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=what-the-bleep">what-the-bleep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=twss">twss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=uber-graphic-extreme">uber-graphic-extreme</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=heart-of-darkness">heart-of-darkness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=woman-in-peril">woman-in-peril</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52705106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3111599250382739702">I struggled with how to rate this book -- from 1 star, to 5 stars, to <i>no stars</i>. There is a part of me that regrets ever having picked up this book, and definitely a part of me that (for better or worse) will never forget reading it. My first visceral reaction to it was that Scott had penned an outrageously exploitative, gratuitous book, one so gruesome in parts, and so fully realized, that I felt like an accomplice, aiding and abetting "Alice's" abductor. The book left me reeling from shock and </span>
  <span id="freeText3111599250382739702" style="display:none">I struggled with how to rate this book -- from 1 star, to 5 stars, to <i>no stars</i>. There is a part of me that regrets ever having picked up this book, and definitely a part of me that (for better or worse) will never forget reading it. My first visceral reaction to it was that Scott had penned an outrageously exploitative, gratuitous book, one so gruesome in parts, and so fully realized, that I felt like an accomplice, aiding and abetting "Alice's" abductor. The book left me reeling from shock and revulsion. Yes, it's that graphic. <br /><br />I will say what I said after reading Jerzy Kosiński's <i>The Painted Bird</i>: "Can people really be that cruel and savage towards one another? Of course they can, I just don't like to be reminded of it especially by a writer with such obvious talents." And Elizabeth Scott is a <i>very talented</i> writer, and in her hands, this story will not just haunt you, but <i>hurt</i> you. <br /><br />Having said that, this is an important book, one that throws a spotlight on a taboo subject we all wish didn't exist. But it does exist, for countless abducted children, and for countless children victimized by family or friends. I had a friend explain to me why she thought this book is so important, and I had to agree with her: this book doesn't make us an <i>accomplice</i>, but rather a <i>witness</i> -- in the reading we are bearing witness to such awful, indescribable crimes, much as we would when reading a book about the Holocaust. You bear witness so that you won't ever forget all those nameless, faceless victims. We bear witness so that maybe next time, we will recognize when something's "not right", we will identify the child in distress who cannot ask for help. <br /><br />I did not enjoy this book; it ranks as one of the most difficult and assaulting reads of my life. But Scott has told an amazing story, giving voice to a voiceless victim, restoring humanity to a young girl who thought she had every bit of hers ripped away. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3111599250382739702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_278584038" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/278584038" />
    <a title="Lora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4632071-lora"><img alt="Lora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305237530p2/4632071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/278584038?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lora" href="/user/show/4632071-lora">Lora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781423397502" href="/book/show/6536599-living-dead-girl">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">not going there</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=lib-audiobooks">lib-audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer278584038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9414080165948045259"><b>Here's what I'd like to know:</b> What made Elizabeth Scott go from Sarah Dessen to Ellen Hopkins and back again? Scott's fourth YA offering, <i>Living Dead Girl</i>, is so far removed from her other works that I'm finding it hard to believe they're even written by the same author. <i>Living Dead Girl</i> is raw and repulsive, whereas all of Scott's other stories are sunshine and butterflies swirling over romantic heads.<br/>When an author begins writing, they usually decide what sort of stories they will write most o</span>
  <span id="freeText9414080165948045259" style="display:none"><b>Here's what I'd like to know:</b> What made Elizabeth Scott go from Sarah Dessen to Ellen Hopkins and back again? Scott's fourth YA offering, <i>Living Dead Girl</i>, is so far removed from her other works that I'm finding it hard to believe they're even written by the same author. <i>Living Dead Girl</i> is raw and repulsive, whereas all of Scott's other stories are sunshine and butterflies swirling over romantic heads.<br />When an author begins writing, they usually decide what sort of stories they will write most often, what genre they'd like to be best known for. Create a brand for themselves, if you will. I just don't know how Scott could go from <i>this</i> to the fluffy chick-lit stories she writes nowadays.<br /><br />It is as if Scott just sat down and started typing the most abhorrent story she could think of. Although the discriptions aren't graphic, the reader knows all too well what is happening to Alice, <b>again</b> and <b>again</b> and <b>
  <i>again</i>
</b>.<br />She is starved in order to be kept small, because when Ray took her she was only ten and is now fifteen. She's allowed to weigh no more than 100 pounds and lives off of mostly yogurt and scraps that he occasionally allows her to have. If it weren't for her sneaking and eating food left by people in their apartment's laundry room and other sorts of hideouts, she'd be dead by now.<br />She is raped — both vaginally and orally — multiple times each day. She lives to serve Ray, is seldom allowed to speak and her education ended when she fell into Ray's clutches. That is, her <i>normal</i> education. With Ray she has been taught all sorts of nasty things.<br />As he would have it, they live under the pretense that he is her father, but of course her real parents are long gone. They live at 623 Daisy Lane, and should Alice ever try to escape from her hell on earth, Ray will go to her parents' house and burn it to the ground.<br />The girl whom Ray had before her, Alice (he names all of his children this; the current Alice's real name isn't revealed until the very end), was killed at fifteen and found floating in the river. The Alice of today figures that he'll surely soon tire of her and pick a new little girl, but every time he threatens her life survival instincts kick in and she begs to be allowed to live. Even though she isn't really living, merely existing.<br /><br />The fact is, with the blunt news stories and knowledge that most people have, it doesn't take a very active imagination to guess at some of the sick things that happen in this world. Therefore I see no point to this story. And it's supposed to be for a teen audience? I'm sorry but, WTF?<br />And I understand that bittersweet absolution is the only form of a happy ending that could work here <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Alice has already begun to show sadistic and masochistic tendencies, and she'd really never be able to live like a normal human and function properly. Still, even though I know it was for the best, I cried knowing that her life had to end after everything she'd been through.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but if there could be something to learn, to take, from this story — other than that paranoia isn't a bad thing when it comes to your children and that the word <i>overprotective</i> should never be applied to a careful parent — I'd be more inclinded to see the reasoning behind the creation of a story such as this. But as it stands, other than scarring the reader for life, I don't see the relevance of this story. <br />And I cannot, in good conscience, say that I actually <i>liked</i> this book and its contents. For that reason, I can give it no more than <b>2.5 stars</b> rounded down to 2.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9414080165948045259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_34816700" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34816700" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/656036-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523497751p2/656036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34816700?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/656036-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who like A Child Called It, also possibly Jailbait</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Susan by: </span>
      talked about on yalsa-bk
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/656036-susan?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer34816700&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34816700" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5601976760150300962">It's hard to say that I liked this book. I am still mulling over it and find it remarkably disturbing. A fictional account of a 15 year old girl, "Alice", who was not always Alice. She used to be a sheltered, spoiled girl until days before her 10th birthday when she is abducted by a sexual predator named Ray. And she is not Ray's first victim--she is terrified into staying with him, despite the fact that he leaves her alone every day to go to work, because he threatens to kill her family if she </span>
  <span id="freeText5601976760150300962" style="display:none">It's hard to say that I liked this book. I am still mulling over it and find it remarkably disturbing. A fictional account of a 15 year old girl, "Alice", who was not always Alice. She used to be a sheltered, spoiled girl until days before her 10th birthday when she is abducted by a sexual predator named Ray. And she is not Ray's first victim--she is terrified into staying with him, despite the fact that he leaves her alone every day to go to work, because he threatens to kill her family if she leaves. He killed the last Alice when she turned 15, as a womanly shape is not to his liking. Then he killed Alice's parents, and well before then he killed his own sexually abusive mother. <br /><br />Now that Alice is 15 she wants nothing more for him to end her life as the living dead girl, the girl who is neither living nor able to die. She is a shell of what she once was. People do not notice her. They have lived in their apartment several years, yet she goes mostly unnoticed. Neighnors even praise Ray's parenting a "different" girl who requires home schooling. However, Ray's plans for her are much more sinister than mere murder. Alice will help him find his next youthful victim, and she will hold her hands while he breaks her in, she will teach the new girl what Ray likes. Initially Alice is more than happy to do this. She is so damaged that rather than being horrifed at this possibily she is anxious to find someone that Ray would rather be with than her, someone to unspoil, show them what the cruel world is like. Alice will steal her food to keep her small - as Alice herself is practically starved to remain a prepubescent 100 pounds who does not menstruate, who does not have hips or breasts.<br /><br />So, Alice finds 6 year old Lucy (whom Ray will call Annabelle) at the park. She also meets Barbara, a police woman who has taken notice of her frail appearance. Over several days time, she seduces Lucy's stoner brother Jake as a distraction so that Ray can take her. But the numbness begins to wear off, and Jake notices Ray watching her and she weakly asks for help. In the end, Jake returns with a gun when Ray tries to grab hold of the screaming Annbelle. He shoots him, thinking himself the hero until he realizes that he's also shot Alice in the stomach -- before dying she tells Jake her real name (which the reader finally learns is Kyla) and address and she collapses underneath Ray's weight and is "finally free".<br /> <br />A devastating as it is, there really was no other way for this story to end happily. Alice is damaged beyond repair, I don't see how she could have recovered and lived a normal life after the 5 years of sexual, physical, and mental abuse she was subjected to. I'm just glad that Ray met his end and that ultimately she met her end because of him it wasn't by his hand. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5601976760150300962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2317866890595301255">Reading this book was a terribly shocking experience! How the author boldly recounts a story of a young girl that is a victim of pedophilia is so vivid and blatant, I was truly horrified. It was horrible to know what Alice (whose real name is Kyla) went through in the hands of the creepy perverted psychopath, Ray (whose actions were also motivated by the same dark past in the hands of a pedophilic mother) and it was painful to see Kyla’s life slip away at 15. The story being short and direct, I </span>
  <span id="freeText2317866890595301255" style="display:none">Reading this book was a terribly shocking experience! How the author boldly recounts a story of a young girl that is a victim of pedophilia is so vivid and blatant, I was truly horrified. It was horrible to know what Alice (whose real name is Kyla) went through in the hands of the creepy perverted psychopath, Ray (whose actions were also motivated by the same dark past in the hands of a pedophilic mother) and it was painful to see Kyla’s life slip away at 15. The story being short and direct, I think has something to do with its main message which is “what happens to little girls who neglect this very important safety rule- never talk to strangers.” <br /><br />One good thing in this story is when Kyla finally finds her voice towards the end of the story enabling her to save a little girl, Lucy from the same ill fate in the hands of Ray. The ending, though abrupt and short gives hope to the readers and to Kyla.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2148082401504231005">I can recognize quality writing when I see it and I have to admit that while I did not like or enjoy (if that is even possible) this book it is well written. This review is not a criticism of the author's writing, she is an excellent writer. <br/><br/>I am usually pretty liberal when it comes to teen books I understand that teen books are often on the cutting edge and pushing the boundaries of comfort for their readers to introduce them to the world we live in. <br/><br/>The reasons for which I gave this book only </span>
  <span id="freeText2148082401504231005" style="display:none">I can recognize quality writing when I see it and I have to admit that while I did not like or enjoy (if that is even possible) this book it is well written. This review is not a criticism of the author's writing, she is an excellent writer. <br /><br />I am usually pretty liberal when it comes to teen books I understand that teen books are often on the cutting edge and pushing the boundaries of comfort for their readers to introduce them to the world we live in. <br /><br />The reasons for which I gave this book only one star are many. On a personal level this book was very disturbing. I read it because it was recommended to me and people I respect believe that it will be a canidate for the awards. I do believe giving it an award would be a mistake. When we give a book an award it is the same as saying this is a great book and I recommend that you read this book. I am concerned that this book is not appropriate for the intended audience. I can not see recommending this book to any teenager--their parents would have my head if I were to do so. One of the reviews I read for this book described it as "vivid not graphic." I have to differ with this opinion. I found the book to be too graphic. <br /><br />Cautions to readers: Abuse of several kinds take place in this book, verbal, physical, and sexual. Very graphic and distubing.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416960607" href="/book/show/6413444-living-dead-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2015">z-read2015</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1773151196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16851346749959558391"><i>Living Dead Girl</i> is one of the most disturbing books I've ever read. It's memorable in its scariness and in its realness. <br/><br/>The protagonist has been the victim of sexual abuse by a much older man for years. Her only hope is to draw another girl into her fate and await her own murder. The author draws you in with an <b>interesting writing style</b> and <b>suspenseful tone,</b> keeping you hooked to the end. Her usage of a dry narrative style with less punctuation really added emotion here. <br/><br/>But this isn't just a </span>
  <span id="freeText16851346749959558391" style="display:none"><i>Living Dead Girl</i> is one of the most disturbing books I've ever read. It's memorable in its scariness and in its realness. <br /><br />The protagonist has been the victim of sexual abuse by a much older man for years. Her only hope is to draw another girl into her fate and await her own murder. The author draws you in with an <b>interesting writing style</b> and <b>suspenseful tone,</b> keeping you hooked to the end. Her usage of a dry narrative style with less punctuation really added emotion here. <br /><br />But this isn't just a cheap thriller; <b>Alice's character is extremely strong.</b> She's borderline sociopathic, but we can see exactly how she got to that point. It's impossible not to sympathize and want her happy. <br /><br />Definitely recommended for fans of both suspense and real-issue contemporaries, because this is somehow both.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3404931044780696986">This is truly a horrific book; one that I want to forget, but probably never will.<br/><br/>The writing is superb, but the content is beyond my cognitive comprehension…truly disturbing, haunting and poignant that propelled me to a level of angst I wasn't prepared to experience. The story was about a 10 year old girl that was abducted from a school trip by a sexual predator. After five ye</span>
  <span id="freeText3404931044780696986" style="display:none">This is truly a horrific book; one that I want to forget, but probably never will.<br /><br />The writing is superb, but the content is beyond my cognitive comprehension…truly disturbing, haunting and poignant that propelled me to a level of angst I wasn't prepared to experience. I was warned to proceed with caution on this book and being the curious person that I am, I didn't listen. BIG.MISTAKE. The story was about a 10 year old girl that was abducted from a school trip by a sexual predator. After five years of being his captive and having been abused in ways I want to forget, Alice is a Living Dead Girl… someone no one sees and more importantly no one saves.<br /><br />Elizabeth Scott brings to the forefront the truth behind the reason abducted victims don't seek help and accept their broken life… one word… fear. I'll never forget the address 623 Daisy Lane… This is the first time I am giving 5 stars to a book I can say I truly hated, but it does deserve the rating... unchartered territory, brutally honest and disturbingly realistic. Not recommended for the faint at heart or young adults, trust me on this.</span>
