<div id="review_35939508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35939508" />
    <a title="Tasha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/929521-tasha"><img alt="Tasha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448392221p2/929521.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35939508?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tasha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tasha" href="/user/show/929521-tasha">Tasha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/929521-tasha?shelf=teen">teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35939508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12070508499351508276">This is one of the most gripping and brutal novels for teens I have ever read. It is the story of Alice, who was abducted as a 10-year-old by Ray, who has sexually and emotionally abused her for five years. Alice knows that if she tries to escape, her entire family will be killed. Now Ray has started starving her to try to maintain her childlike body, not allowing her to get over 100 pounds. His violence is also increasing as are his death threats. Alice has long wanted to die, but death eludes </span>
  <span id="freeText12070508499351508276" style="display:none">This is one of the most gripping and brutal novels for teens I have ever read. It is the story of Alice, who was abducted as a 10-year-old by Ray, who has sexually and emotionally abused her for five years. Alice knows that if she tries to escape, her entire family will be killed. Now Ray has started starving her to try to maintain her childlike body, not allowing her to get over 100 pounds. His violence is also increasing as are his death threats. Alice has long wanted to die, but death eludes her time and again though she wishes for it often. Ray now wants a new little girl to join them, so Alice is allowed to head to a park and start scouting for what she can only hope will be her replacement.<br /><br />This is a book that makes you want to scream. It's depictions of the horrors of Alice's life are so plainly laid out, unflinchingly documented, and horribly vivid. Scott's writing can be poetic at times, underlining the brutality and desperation of the book. Her pacing is perfection, leaving readers gasping for air as the oppressive nature of the story becomes too much. This is a book that you will set down, only to return to immediately. It is a book that will linger in your mind, enter your dreams, and change the way you see. It is a book that is brutal truth that we often turn away from. It is suffocating, dreadful, horrific and supremely, magically human all at the same time.<br /><br />Heart-wrenching in its honesty, this book will appeal to many teens. Hand it to the fans of A Child Called It. Appropriate for ages 16-18.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12070508499351508276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_197268921" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197268921" />
    <a title="lauren ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3866561-lauren"><img alt="lauren ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597732137p2/3866561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/197268921?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lauren ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lauren ♡" href="/user/show/3866561-lauren">lauren ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416960607" href="/book/show/6413444-living-dead-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3866561-lauren?shelf=genre-contemporary">genre-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3866561-lauren?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3866561-lauren?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3866561-lauren?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer197268921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1971716875115695948"><a href='https://wonderlessreviews.wordpress.com/2016/08/18/review-living-dead-girl-by-elizabeth-scott/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Read this review @ my blog Wonderless Reviews</a><br/><br/><b>Trigger warning:</b> This book includes graphic violence and rape scenes and deals with pedophilia.<br/><br/>I often start my reviews by saying, “I’m not quite sure how to review this” but when I say this about Living Dead Girl I truly mean it. This is one of the most upsetting and disturbing books I’ve ever read.<br/><br/>I added Living Dead Girl to my TBR on Goodreads years ago so when I found it out a local library sale for 50c I bought and read it right away. I knew noth</span>
  <span id="freeText1971716875115695948" style="display:none"><a href="https://wonderlessreviews.wordpress.com/2016/08/18/review-living-dead-girl-by-elizabeth-scott/" rel="nofollow noopener">Read this review @ my blog Wonderless Reviews</a><br /><br /><b>Trigger warning:</b> This book includes graphic violence and rape scenes and deals with pedophilia.<br /><br />I often start my reviews by saying, “I’m not quite sure how to review this” but when I say this about Living Dead Girl I truly mean it. This is one of the most upsetting and disturbing books I’ve ever read.<br /><br />I added Living Dead Girl to my TBR on Goodreads years ago so when I found it out a local library sale for 50c I bought and read it right away. I knew nothing about this book other than the vague blurb implied an abduction and that its Goodreads reviews all talked about how creepy it was. I presumed it would follow a similar pattern to most YA books that deal with this subject and having read one of Elizabeth Scott’s other books Bloom (which was quiet terrible) I wasn’t expecting much. I couldn’t have been more wrong.<br /><br />The plot centers around a girl named “Alice” who was abducted by a man called Ray five years ago when she was a child. We see Alice’s day-to-day struggles having to deal with Ray’s physical and emotional abuse. Ray decides Alice is no longer young enough and sets her a task to abduct a new girl and everything spirals from there.<br /><br /><blockquote>“Three life lessons:<br />1.No one will see you.<br />2.No one will say anything.<br />3.No one will save you.”</blockquote><br /><br />You will feel so many emotions reading this book. Even if you’re not an empathetic person it’ll be hard not to – at some stage in this book – empathise with Alice. This book will break your heart.<br /><br />The thing that hit me the hardest with Living Dead Girl was how utterly realistic it was. I felt like I was reading somebody’s personal memoir. A lot of times these themes can be romanticised or used for shock value, but this book was like someone poured their heart and soul into writing about an experience they actually went through. Elizabeth Scott handled these subjects as brilliantly as someone could when dealing with such sensitive topics. I normally love dark books and it takes a lot to get to me, but boy did this book get to me. It was extremely confronting and brutal. As much as we don’t want to think about it awful things like this happen all the time and we are all blissfully oblivious and unaware. This is highlighted by the opening paragraph were we’re in the point of view of a random inhabitant of the complex where Ray and Alice are who just presumes Ray is Alice’s father and that Alice is his “ungrateful” teenage daughter.<br /><br /><blockquote>“I don’t understand why my shell keeps living. Breathing. Why won’t it listen to me, to the little part I have that isn’t Ray, to that tiny once upon a time girl who just wants to close her eyes and never wake up again?”</blockquote><br /><br />Living Dead Girl is more a character study on victims and their attackers. We really get into the mind of Alice and feel everything she feels. Ray allows Alice to leave their appartment as long as she follows the rules he gives her. He threatens that he’ll kill her parents if she doesn’t listen. As a reader you may be frustrated by the amount of times Alice is able to seemingly rescue herself from the situation she’s in but doesn’t. I actually appreciated this though because I think people underestimate the power of emotional abuse and in Alice’s case it’s been amplified by Stockholm Syndrome and physical/sexual abuse. Ray has told Alice over and over again since she was a child that if she doesn’t obey him her family would die. Her believing him is heartbreakingly accurate.<br /><br />One of the saddest things, besides having to witness all the trauma Alice goes through, is seeing her will and strength constantly build up and then be broken down. She’ll start feeling determined about escaping, but then of course the years of abuse she’d suffered comes back and she will shrink down and admit defeat. Or, on a more confronting sense of strength she’ll wish for death and want Ray to kill her, but then she’ll give up on that too.<br /><br /><blockquote>“I am the living dead girl because I am too weak to die.”</blockquote><br /><br />It seems wrong to talk about this book in a technical sense, but despite the lack of plot the chapters are all really short and so fast paced that it’s impossible not to read this book in one sitting. The writing is poetic, but done in a way without romanticising the situation. I know some people have a problem with the abuse that Alice suffers being “too” descriptive, but someone who has experienced this thing in real life didn’t have the privilege of having them sugarcoated so why should we? I understand people’s concerns when abuse is used as a plot device and in that sense I agree, but with how realistic this book is it was definitely justified.<br /><br />My review is shorter than usual because there’s nothing else I can really say without giving away the ending. This book is not an easy read. No review or anything I say will even be enough to prepare you, but if you can deal with these subject matters I can’t recommend it enough. One of the reasons this book affected me so much was because I have young siblings and the thought of this happening to them made me feel sick. Then I remembered that these thing have happened to someone’s sibling or child or friend. Just because these issues are confronting and truly awful doesn’t mean we should forget they exist or not talk about them. I appreciate Elizabeth Scott for talking about this in a way that was respectful and realistic and making 170 pages hit me harder than any other full length novel that I’ve read. There is no way I can give this book any less than 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1971716875115695948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/679025-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323234939p2/679025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/282338440?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/679025-penny">Penny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282338440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4484658312837728136">A difficult book for a mother of three little girls to read. Frightening. Devastating. Heartbreaking. I hate this book because it made me feel so much,<i> too much</i>. Reduced me to genuine sobs, as if I was mourning the passing of a loved one. This story will haunt me forever. I am able appreciate Living Dead Girl for these reasons.<br/><br/>Regardless of the content, the subject matter, Living Dead Girl is well-crafted. Every word has a purpose, every sentence deliberate. The imagery is in-your-face, brazen, </span>
  <span id="freeText4484658312837728136" style="display:none">A difficult book for a mother of three little girls to read. Frightening. Devastating. Heartbreaking. I hate this book because it made me feel so much,<i> too much</i>. Reduced me to genuine sobs, as if I was mourning the passing of a loved one. This story will haunt me forever. I am able appreciate Living Dead Girl for these reasons.<br /><br />Regardless of the content, the subject matter, Living Dead Girl is well-crafted. Every word has a purpose, every sentence deliberate. The imagery is in-your-face, brazen, yet at the same time it's so subtle. I don't know how Elizabeth Scott managed to do that. How many other authors <i>can</i> do that? Clearly Scott knows what she's doing. She possesses rare gift. Four stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4484658312837728136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34141146?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/214822-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of short, depressing books like John Steinbeck's &quot;The Pearl&quot;</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/214822-donna?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/214822-donna?shelf=teen">teen</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34141146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12128580643925688822"><i>I had to update this review after reading comments by other people about the book.</i> I hated, hated, hated the ending of this book. I would have given it 3 stars if the ending didn't make me so angry. I haven't been this pissed off at a book in a long time. I realize that a lot of people disagree, and they're welcome to their own opinions. I just did not like it. Does that mean it's not worth reading? No. I liked it up until the end, and it does provoke interesting discussions, so I'm not going to</span>
  <span id="freeText12128580643925688822" style="display:none"><i>I had to update this review after reading comments by other people about the book.</i> I hated, hated, hated the ending of this book. I would have given it 3 stars if the ending didn't make me so angry. I haven't been this pissed off at a book in a long time. I realize that a lot of people disagree, and they're welcome to their own opinions. I just did not like it. Does that mean it's not worth reading? No. I liked it up until the end, and it does provoke interesting discussions, so I'm not going to tell anyone NOT to read it.<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT SPOILER ALERT SPOILER ALERT SPOILER ALERT<br /><br />Some people think the protagonist is alive at the end, others (like me) think that she dies. I think that the way she dies is really lame, too. Basically, it's like the book is saying, "If you've been kidnapped and abused for five years, then you're better off dead."<br /><br />What? Really? There's no chance for rehabilitation? No hope of being reunited with your family? Or of having at least a semi-normal life?</span>

<div id="review_1254539567" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1254539567" />
    <a title="pink (not just another shade of red)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30212137-pink-not-just-another-shade-of-red"><img alt="pink (not just another shade of red)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464612660p2/30212137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1254539567?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="pink (not just another shade of red)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="pink (not just another shade of red)" href="/user/show/30212137-pink-not-just-another-shade-of-red">pink (not just another shade of red)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30212137-pink-not-just-another-shade-of-red?shelf=all-the-26-book-challengr">all-the-26-book-challengr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30212137-pink-not-just-another-shade-of-red?shelf=about-or-with-death-suicide-whatnot">about-or-with-death-suicide-whatnot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30212137-pink-not-just-another-shade-of-red?shelf=horror-disturbing-morbid">horror-disturbing-morbid</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1254539567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6465327464458876771">Some books entertain. Some amaze. Some scare. Some bore. The lines are always clear. We almost always know what kind of books we had in hand. We have many ways to help us define them. Genres.Publisher. Author. Reviews. Star-ratings.<br/>This book,however,transcends lines. It's the kind that tears. The kind that gnaws at your subconscious in the middle of the night. On one hand,the writing is excellent and so very effective. The world built solidly. The characters so real you won't be surprised if the</span>
  <span id="freeText6465327464458876771" style="display:none">Some books entertain. Some amaze. Some scare. Some bore. The lines are always clear. We almost always know what kind of books we had in hand. We have many ways to help us define them. Genres.Publisher. Author. Reviews. Star-ratings.<br />This book,however,transcends lines. It's the kind that tears. The kind that gnaws at your subconscious in the middle of the night. On one hand,the writing is excellent and so very effective. The world built solidly. The characters so real you won't be surprised if they grabbed you by the hand and pull you into the pages. The plot seamless. If we are only to consider Elizabeth Scotts immense talent this book would easily get a 5star rating.<br />On the other hand,there's the fact that this must be one of the most disturbing book ever written. Yes, the very dark and dangerous materials were handled so well. But. That's. The. Point. Exactly. This brilliant author did such a spectacular job in creating such a horrific and painful atmosphere of being trapped,abused, and hurt that I feel utterly suffocated just by reading all about it. And the violence is too much. Too much. I'm aware those kind of horrible things are possibly happening to some helpless,little girls somewhere but that just made me more sick. The villain of this book is simply beyond description. He's the kind I'd enjoy killing brutally if he were a real person and standing in front of me. (Though God forbid!!!) Yet the evil of this is nothing like fictional evil, no mutated giant rats invading the earth nor zombies looking like Abercrombie slash Fitch tempting teenage girls to join the dark them to the dark side. No,this is the kind of simple,sick everyday evil. The kind that makes you cringe. The kind that makes you want to close your eyes. It's like that with this book,you know that feeling of being fascinated with a video of a carcrash. All the time I'm going nonono can't take this anymore!but keep on turning the pages. Thank God the book is only a few pages. It's over soon. The last chapter left me stunned.<br />In my mind I'm screaming You Are Free Now! Please! Stop! You're free...<br />What? What did you say?<br />I am free.<br />Just like that,like a final blow in the gut.<br /><br />So... I'm wondering how could this one possibly be nominated for all those children's and teen's stuff reading selections and such because personally I won't advise anyone below 15 to read this without adult supervision or something. But I still can't find it in my heart to give it lower than 3 stars because Scott is such a talented writer. So three stars. More like 2.5.....Ok,3.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6465327464458876771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_40652354" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40652354" />
    <a title="Arminzerella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1769011-arminzerella"><img alt="Arminzerella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275503782p2/1769011.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40652354?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arminzerella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arminzerella" href="/user/show/1769011-arminzerella">Arminzerella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=sexual-abuse">sexual-abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=abduction">abduction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=rape">rape</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769011-arminzerella?shelf=horrifying">horrifying</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer40652354&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40652354" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8356319224658329910">When “Alice” was a little girl, she was taken by a stranger while she was on a field trip to the aquarium. The man, Ray, offered to reunite her with her classmates, but ended up taking her to his car and bringing her to his home. There, he sexually abused her as his mother had once abused him. When she’d told him who she was and where her parents lived, he threatened to murder them if she ever told anyone what he’d done to her. Alice had to live with this man until she was fifteen. By then she w</span>
  <span id="freeText8356319224658329910" style="display:none">When “Alice” was a little girl, she was taken by a stranger while she was on a field trip to the aquarium. The man, Ray, offered to reunite her with her classmates, but ended up taking her to his car and bringing her to his home. There, he sexually abused her as his mother had once abused him. When she’d told him who she was and where her parents lived, he threatened to murder them if she ever told anyone what he’d done to her. Alice had to live with this man until she was fifteen. By then she was growing into a young woman, which made Ray angry. He wanted her to stay a little girl forever and forced her to wear children’s clothing, starved her so she wouldn’t grow or menstruate, and sent her out to have her body waxed so that she’d remain smooth and hairless. Alice only wants Ray to leave her alone and she doesn’t really care how she achieves that goal. So, when Ray suggests that Alice help him find a new little girl to play with, she’s all for it – anything to redirect his attention away from her. She selects a girl at the park for Ray and they begin planning how they’ll take her. A tiny, fragile hope blooms in Alice that Ray will let her go once he has a new distraction.<br /><br />This was one of the most chilling things I’ve read in a long time. Alice’s situation was both terrible and painful, and while the acts her captor committed on her mind and body weren’t detailed in all of their graphic horror, it was bad enough to imagine what took place between the words. Alice loathes what she has become and does everything to make herself unattractive to Ray – without making him so angry that he punishes her. It doesn’t matter, though. Everything makes him angry, and whatever he does to her is punishment – whether she’s actually been bad or not. His “love” is punishment. The depth of Alice’s apathy is frightening. She’s truly been turned into some kind of warped husk of what she used to be.<br /><br />When Alice convinces Ray to take the little girl in the park, it’s incredibly creepy just how willing she is to sacrifice that child’s innocence and happiness to save herself. And not even to save herself for anything. She has no plans to better herself, no plans to find help, no plans for her future except to get away from Ray. Up until she tells the girl to run, it seems that Alice is trapped in the vicious cycle of abuse (and if this were a V.C. Andrews novel, the sequel would bear that out), and that she is going to be its next perpetrator. Alice’s would-be savior shoots Ray as he comes for Alice and the little girl. Ray goes down, but so does Alice. And this is her dream ending – relief, bliss, final release. She’s so destroyed that only death brings her the peace that she longs for. I wondered (hopefully, you will, too) whether Alice could have made it on her own if she’d gotten away, gotten some kind of help. There’s a cop who gives her information about a center for girls who are in some kind of trouble, and readers will hope that she somehow finds the courage to go there, to get the assistance she needs. But Alice has made her attempts at reaching out, and the adults in her life up until this point have all failed her. Is she now so broken that she’ll never be able to live a normal life? Probably. That’s saddest of all.<br /><br />Teens (especially teenage girls) will probably eat up this cautionary tale. And then, cast quick looks over their shoulders as they scurry past the shadows. This is the stuff of horror – all the more horrific because we know that it happens. Children disappear all the time – many to unknown fates. It’s almost impossible not to be affected/moved by this book. It will (and should!) horrify you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8356319224658329910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4IfGETLgIPiOXzZDc+iOV7WtIrB3axCVT7J2s1xF1ZkOC5LrsPQI2w1m04nWJ0T9NJpeMFWLgbqA7Oy7+buOCw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XBe4f7B5D3xMc/CFeeL/f3aSAkDogmINAUfJ957sftqym+yFMm0nX89KFU/cLTXV96V+wMpi8yLOGVP/OxIlSA==')})
  }
